as New York, London, Hong Kong, Singapore, Sydney, Melbourne, Frankfurt and Dubai.</P>\n<P><BR></P>\n<H2>So, Want To Learn How He Did It?</H2>\n<P>In this 4-week, <STRONG><EM>live</EM></STRONG> online customer\u00a0</P>\n</LI>\n<LI>\n<P>Identifying gaps in the market</P>\n</LI>\n<LI>\n<P>Why timing is everything</P>\n</LI>\n<LI>\n<P><SPAN>Building your funnel</SPAN></P>\n</LI>\n<LI>\n<P>Lean marketing 101</P>\n</LI>\n<LI>\n<P>A growth hacker mindset</P>\n</LI>\n<LI>\n<P>Using lead magnets effectively</P>\n</LI>\n<LI>\n<P>Amplifying your lead generation</P>\n</LI>\n<LI>\n<P>Sales and marketing tools</P>\n</LI>\n<LI>\n<P>The power of automation and outsourcing</P>\n</LI>\n<LI>\n<P>Qualifying and prioritizing leads</P>\n</LI>\n<LI>\n<P>Closing deals</P>\n</LI>\n<LI>\n<P>Referrals and up-sells</P>\n</LI>\n</UL>\n<P><BR></P>\n<H2>Who Should Enrol</H2>\n<P><SPAN>This course is not just for entrepreneurs and startups. </SPAN></P>\n<P><SPAN>The techniques and tools delivered, are 8:30am AEST /\u00a0<SPAN>(GMT Thursday 13 June, 9pm - 10:30pm)</SPAN></P>\n<H2></H2>\n<H2>Course Delivery</H2>\n<P>This course will take place entirely online, via live stream webinar, and all participants will be able to engage with the facilitator and each other in real time.</P>\n<P>A number of activities will be presented to participants for completion in between each session in order                 "text": "The Urban Developer\u2019s Residential Development Summit is the ultimate one-day download of the latest research, expert perspective, case studies and site tours for residential property developers and professionals.\nThis exclusive 100-member only summit will explore the fundamental supply and demand dynamics of the high-density, medium-density and greenfield land markets within each of our three host cities - Brisbane, Sydney and Melbourne.\nBy drawing upon the perspective of leading developers within these markets, the summit will also identify the key issues facing the residential development industry over the coming years.\nIndividual sessions relating to the high-density unit market, greenfield land market and the boutique owner-occupier market will provide specific context and analysis of each of these sub-markets.\nThe summit will put a spotlight on the key players taking advantage of market corrections, project strategies for developing in a challenging environment, the impact of financing and new funding models, shifting development site values and changing buyer profiles.\nThe event will conclude with an afternoon of interactive site tours from award-winning developers within each of the cities.\nThis is a unique opportunity for a select group of developers and professionals to come together and develop a deeper understanding of the major forces shaping the residential development sector into the immediate future.\n\n\n\nAGENDA:\n8.00am - Registrations and networking\n8.30am - Opening remarks and sponsor acknowledgement\u00a0\n8.40am - STATE OF THE MARKET: A sector-by-sector based research perspective on supply, demand and everything in between -\u00a0A detailed briefing from leading property researchers into the apartment, townhouse and greenfield land markets in your city. In this session, we will explore the key supply and demand dynamics of each sub-market and identify the areas for future development activity.\nSpeakers: Cameron Kusher -\u00a0Head of Research - Australia, Corelogic\n\n9.00am - 2020: A DEVELOPER'S PERSPECTIVE:\u00a0Inside the mindset of how these property developers are approaching the next two years -\u00a0A moderated panel discussion with key developers from across the residential sector. In this session, we will explore how these developers are approaching the coming years and identify the key locations, product types, price points, project sizes and strategies that they are deploying.\nSpeakers: Lucy Simms - Senior Development Manager, Perri Projects | Len Warson - CEO, Glenvill | more to come...\n\n9.40am - GREENFIELD - GLAMOUR OR GLOOM? What is the outlook for the greenfield development market over the next two years? -\u00a0In this session, we will explore the state of the greenfield development sector from the perspective of several key operators. Join us as we hear from experts who will provide perspective on product mix, buyer profiles, sales strategies, project financing, product design, marketing strategies and more.\u00a0\u00a0\nSpeakers: Liz Ronson - Managing Director, Jinding Developments |\u00a0Luke Kelly - Director, RPM Real Estate Group\n\n10.20am - Morning Tea\n\n10.40am - UNITS RISING FROM THE ASHES: What is the outlook for the inner-city high-density unit market over the next two years? -\u00a0In this session, we will be joined by experts from across the spectrum of the high-density unit market to assess what the outlook is for this sector in the coming years. The session will explore buyer demand, settlement risk, sales strategies, site values, project financing and residual stock opportunities.\nSpeakers: Kerren McNamara - Managing Director, KIN Property | Jozef Dickinson - Director, Residential, Colliers International | Andrew Hogan - Managing Director, Point Polaris | more to come...\n\n11.20am - THE BOUTIQUE BONANZA: How the death of the investor and the rise of the owner occupier is giving birth to a new wave of premium boutique development.\u00a0- In this session we will hear from active participants within the boutique development sector and explore the changing nature of the owner occupier market. The discussion will consider buyer profiles, design and product finishes, marketing strategies, financing models and construction considerations.\nSpeakers: Michael Fox - Managing Director, Costa Fox | Miriam Fanning - Founder & Principal, MIM Design | Tim Lowe - Managing Director, Lowe Group |\u00a0Chris McCue - Director Architecture, Carr\n\n12.00pm - Closing remarks & Light lunch/networking\n2.00pm - 4:00pm\u00a0SITE TOURS\u00a0\n\n\n\nWHO SHOULD ATTEND?\n\n\nResidential property developers\n\n\nDevelopment site owners\n\n\nProperty investors considering property development\n\n\nArchitects, engineers and professional consultants\n\n\nTown planning, government and planning authorities\n\n\nBanks, brokers and finance professionals\n\n\nReal estate agents, project marketers and selling channels\n\n\nConstruction contractors and subcontractors \n\n\nOther service providers to the industry\n\n\nTechnology and marketing businesses\n\n\nProduct and building suppliers\n\n\n\n\n\n\n",

                "text": "Agile software development is based on principles defined by the Agile Manifesto; a disciplined project management outline that is conducive to dynamic inspection and adaptation. Agile methods include many product development frameworks such as Scrum and XP (eXtreme Programming) which allow for rapid delivery of software. The Scrum framework uses simple iterative practices for team collaboration on complex projects.\n\u00a0Our 8 hours of training offer an overview of Agile development and Scrum practices, focusing on how the Scrum framework follows the Agile Manifesto principles. Learn how to harness complex processes and apply Scrum techniques to an IT and/or non-IT project, through a blended combination of slide-based lecture and interactive case studies. Students gain practical advice, with real world simulation exercises that can align traditional project management to the agile route.\n\u00a0Certification\nOn successful completion of the course, you It includes planning and preparing for a critique using techniques that ensure that the person receiving the criticism is motivated to rectify past mistakes and work towards improvement. \u00a0Learn skills like reading body language, when and where to give a critique, correct tone and much more.\r\nThis dynamic and practical training course is now available throughout Australia, including Brisbane, Parramatta Sydney, Melbourne, Adelaide, Canberra, Parramatta and Perth and also via instructor-led online training.\r\nLearning Outcomes\r\n\r\nDetermine the right place to give feedback\r\nConsider informal feedback\r\nGather facts on the issue\r\nPractice tone\r\nCriticise in private, praise in public\r\nCreate a safe environment for providing criticism\r\nMonitor body language\r\nDevelop understanding and active listening\r\nBe collaborative\r\nCheck emotions and outbursts\r\nDiffuse negative emotions including anger\r\nUnderstand what not to do\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nCourse Outline\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nDelivering Constructive Criticism Training Course -                 "text": "\u00a0\r\nSuicide prevention training\r\nInformed by the latest research in suicide prevention, Wesley LifeForce training equips participants with a variety of skills such as managing suicidal crisis, understanding risk and protective factors, as well as how to recognise potential warning signs. We offer both full-day workshops and half-day seminars. Our programs are aimed at training individuals from all walks of life, as well as organisational groups.\r\nThe training\r\nWesley LifeForce has developed quality suicide prevention training. Our Suicide Prevention Workshop is designed to teach people how to identify the signs that someone may be at risk of suicide and appropriate action to take. Simple effective interventions can make a real difference and save lives. All Wesley LifeForce facilitators are accredited trainers and have completed suicide intervention training. Many are also accredited counsellors.\r\nCommunity information resources\r\nWhen faced with a crisis, individuals often do not know how to access appropriate assistance.\u00a0 With this in mind, Wesley LifeForce has developed \u2018community information cards\u2019 and \u2018community information posters\u2019. Every workshop participant receives a community information card which includes national 24-hour crisis numbers and information about local community services/resources.\r\nEnsuring participant safety\r\nAll workshop material is specifically designed with participant\u2019s safety in mind. Our course material is vetted by MindFrame \u2013 an Australian Government body which provides expert advice to the Suicide Prevention Sector on responsible reporting/portrayal of the issue of suicide.\r\nThe outcomes\r\n\r\nunderstand risk and protective factors\r\nhow to identify the warning signs that someone may be at risk of suicide\r\nhow to ask directly about suicide intent.\r\nunderstand what local and national support and resources are available to support a person at risk.\r\n",

Our Suicide Prevention Workshop is designed to teach people how to identify the signs that someone may be at risk of suicide and appropriate action to take. Simple effective interventions can make a real difference and save lives. All Wesley LifeForce facilitators are accredited trainers and have completed suicide intervention training. Many are also accredited counsellors.</P>\r\n<H2>Community information resources</H2>\r\n<P>When faced with a crisis, individuals often do not know how to access appropriate assistance.\u00a0 With this in mind, Wesley LifeForce has developed \u2018community information cards\u2019 and \u2018community information posters\u2019. He is passionate about delivering a fantastic employee experience through data driven techniques and practising design thinking.Course CurriculumModule 1: Organisational structure and what is culture\n\nA deeper understanding of what culture and how it impacts revenue and cost\nIdentifying the key drivers of your culture, how has it changed and how will it change\nEvaluate your company\u2019s current culture and what you would like it to be\nCase studies of culture at top high growth startups\nTechniques to achieve quick wins to improve your company culture\nDevelop a long-term plan with steps you can action immediately\n\nModule 2: How recruitment affects company performance and how to set it up for success\n\nWhat does best fit talent look like?\nWhat is a good recruitment process?\nInterview training - how to set your team up to interview well\nThe recruitment ecosystem and how to source the best talent\nHow to work with vendors, overview of different distribution channels\u00a0\nWhat is your employer brand and why it is important?\n\nModule 3: Leadership, accountability and performance\n\nAs a leader in your business, what is your role and responsibility?\nHow does your leadership team change, when and why?\nPerformance management - how do people know what they are accountable for?\nSetting up good communication channels and setting up a pro feedback culture\nDevelop a culture of collaboration and learning. Post exiting his own startup, Mahesh joined Canva and established the People and Culture function. In 2016 Canva was named \u2018Best place to work\u2019 by Job Advisor. How to continually upskill your team on a low budget.</LI>\n</UL>\n<P><BR><STRONG>Module 4: People analytics, incentive architecture, decision making and diversity</STRONG><BR></P>\n<UL>\n<LI>Understand the value of diversity, how to promote diversity in your teams and decision making\u00a0</LI>\n<LI>Overview of current HR systems, when to invest into them based on the different stages of growth</LI>\n<LI>Designing HR policy and guidelines to motivate your people and how these change will as you grow</LI>\n<LI>What are the People numbers that you should be aware of and what should they be?</LI>\n<LI>What is behavioural economics and how can you nudge behaviours</LI>\n</UL>\n<P><STRONG>Workshop logistics:</STRONG><BR>This is a one-day workshop and is limited to twelve participants, enabling us to focus on your business.
